21/03/2025, 9:17 pm - Yamini: import heapq

def getMaximumAmount(quantity, m):
    # Convert quantity list into a max heap (use negative values since heapq is a min-heap)
    max_heap = [-q for q in quantity]
    heapq.heapify(max_heap)
    
    revenue = 0
    
    # Sell m items, always picking the most valuable one
    for _ in range(m):
        max_value = -heapq.heappop(max_heap)  # Get the highest value item
        revenue += max_value
        
        if max_value - 1 > 0:
            heapq.heappush(max_heap, -(max_value - 1))  # Push the updated value back
    
    return revenue

# Taking input
n = int(input())  # Number of item types
quantity = [int(input()) for _ in range(n)]  # Quantities of each item type
m = int(input())  # Number of customers

# Compute and print the maximum revenue
print(getMaximumAmount(quantity, m))
21/03/2025, 9:17 pm - Yamini: 1
21/03/2025, 9:17 pm - Yamini: def kthOccurrence(X, arr, query_values):
    # Find all occurrences of X in arr and store their indices (1-based)
    occurrences = []
    
    for i, num in enumerate(arr):
        if num == X:
            occurrences.append(i + 1)  # Store 1-based index
    
    result = []
    
    # Process each query
    for q in query_values:
        if q <= len(occurrences):  # Check if the q-th occurrence exists
            result.append(occurrences[q - 1])
        else:
            result.append(-1)
    
    return result

# Taking input
X = int(input())  # The number to search for
n = int(input())  # Size of array
arr = [int(input()) for _ in range(n)]  # Array elements
q = int(input())  # Number of queries
query_values = [int(input()) for _ in range(q)]  # Queries

# Compute and print results
for res in kthOccurrence(X, arr, query_values):
    print(res)

14/04/2025, 7:36 pm - Yamini: #include <stdio.h>
#include <string.h>
#include <ctype.h>

// Function to check if the input is a valid positive integer
int isPositiveInteger(char *str) {
    int len = strlen(str);

    // Empty string check
    if (len == 0) return 0;

    // If the first character is not between '1' and '9', reject (to avoid "0" or "012")
    if (str[0] < '1' || str[0] > '9') {
        return 0;
    }

    // All remaining characters must be digits (0-9)
    for (int i = 1; i < len; i++) {
        if (!isdigit(str[i])) {
            return 0;
        }
    }

    return 1; // Valid positive integer
}

int main() {
    char input[100];

    printf("Enter a string: ");
    fgets(input, sizeof(input), stdin);
    input[strcspn(input, "\n")] = '\0';  // Remove newline character

    if (isPositiveInteger(input)) {
        printf("The input is a valid positive integer.\n");
    } else {
        printf("Invalid input. Not a valid positive integer.\n");
    }

    return 0;
}

16/04/2025, 11:59 am - Yamini: 1. **Two popular CNN architectures:**
   - **VGGNet** (e.g., VGG16, VGG19)
   - **ResNet** (e.g., ResNet50, ResNet101)

2. **BPTT in RNNs:**
   - **BPTT** stands for **Backpropagation Through Time**. It is a training algorithm used to compute gradients for RNNs by unfolding them in time and applying backpropagation.

3. **Two main components of a GAN (Generative Adversarial Network):**
   - **Generator**
   - **Discriminator**

4. **Data augmentation in the context of GANs:**
   - It refers to **synthetically generating new data samples** using the GAN's generator to **expand and diversify the training dataset**, improving the performance of models trained on that data.

5. **Network used for fine-tuning in transfer learning:**
   - **Pre-trained network** (e.g., models like **ResNet**, **Inception**, or **BERT** in NLP) is fine-tuned by updating its weights on a new, often smaller, target dataset.

20/04/2025, 7:03 pm - Yamini: Graph-Based Testing Methods

Steps in Graph-Based Testing:

1. Understand the Objects
Identify the key elements (objects) in the software to be tested.


2. Define Relationships
Determine how these objects interact with or relate to each other.


3. Create a Graph

Nodes represent objects.

Links represent relationships.

Node weights describe properties of nodes.

Link weights describe characteristics of links.



4. Graph Representation

Use directed links (arrows) for one-way relationships.

Use undirected or symmetric links for mutual relationships.

Use parallel links if multiple types of relationships exist between the same nodes.



5. Generate Test Cases

Traverse the graph to create test cases.

Ensure each object and relationship is covered to detect errors.





---

Types of Graph-Based Modeling Methods:

1. Transaction Flow Modeling
Represents steps in a transaction (e.g., airline booking), and links show the flow of the transaction.


2. Finite State Modeling
Nodes are different states/screens of the software. Links are transitions between states.


3. Data Flow Modeling
Nodes are data objects. Links are data transformations (e.g., tax calculation).


4. Timing Modeling
Nodes are program objects. Links are sequences and timings of execution.
20/04/2025, 7:03 pm - Yamini: <Media omitted>
20/04/2025, 7:03 pm - Yamini: <Media omitted>
20/04/2025, 7:03 pm - Yamini: <Media omitted>
20/04/2025, 7:03 pm - Yamini: Orthogonal Array Testing - Simple Points

1. Used When Input is Limited
Best for situations with a small but non-trivial number of input values.


2. Not Suitable for Exhaustive Testing
If testing all combinations is too much, this method helps cover important combinations efficiently.


3. Focuses on Combinations
Instead of testing all values one-by-one, it tests combinations of input values.


4. Uses a Special Structure (Array)
An orthogonal array (like L9) ensures inputs are evenly spread out across test cases.


5. Finds Region Faults
It helps detect region faults—errors that occur only in specific combinations of inputs.


6. Efficient and Balanced Testing
Ensures uniform coverage without testing every possible case.


7. L9 Orthogonal Array Example

3 parameters (X, Y, Z), each with 3 values → 27 combinations.

L9 array reduces this to 9 test cases but still covers the combinations smartly.



8. Better Than One-by-One Testing
The method gives better coverage than testing one input at a time (as shown in the figure).

21/04/2025, 8:40 am - Yamini: Sure, here's a slightly more elaborated version of the four main software testing strategies:


---

1. Unit Testing

Purpose: Test individual components (like functions or classes) in isolation to ensure they perform as expected.

Performed By: Developers

Tools: JUnit (Java), PyTest (Python), NUnit (.NET)

Example: Testing a function that calculates the total bill with tax in a shopping cart module.



---

2. Integration Testing

Purpose: Verify the interaction between multiple components or systems.

Focus: Data flow and control between modules.

Approaches: Top-down, Bottom-up, Big Bang

Tools: Postman (for API), REST Assured, Selenium (for UI)

Example: Testing if the login module correctly redirects to the user dashboard.



---

3. Validation Testing

Purpose: Ensure the software meets the business and user requirements.

Involves: Acceptance testing, functional testing, UI testing.

Performed By: QA engineers or end users

Tools: Cucumber, TestRail

Example: Validating that an e-commerce checkout process meets all user scenarios as defined by the client.



---

4. System Testing

Purpose: Test the complete, integrated application in a real-world environment.

Scope: End-to-end functionality, performance, security, and usability.

Tools: Selenium, TestNG, QTP/UFT

29/06/2025, 11:32 am - Syam: int get_ans(int n, int m, int cols, vector<vector<int> > edges) {
    // Write your code here
    vector<vector<int>> g(n + 1);
    for (const auto& e : edges) {
        int u = e[0], v = e[1];
        g[u].push_back(v);
        g[v].push_back(u);
    }
    vector<int> tin(n + 1), tout(n + 1);
    int timer = 0;
    function<void(int, int)> dfs = [&](int u, int p) {
        tin[u] = timer++;
        for (int v : g[u])
            if (v != p) dfs(v, u);
        tout[u] = timer - 1;
    };
    dfs(1, 0);
    vector<vector<int>> divisiors(n + 1);
    for (int d = 1; d <= n; d++)
        for (int mul = d; mul <= n; mul += d)
    divisiors[mul].push_back(d);
    long long ans = 0;
    for (int u = 1; u <= n; u++)
        for (int v : divisiors[u])
            if (tin[u] <= tin[v] && tin[v] <= tout[u]) ans++;
    return static_cast<int>(ans);
}

29/06/2025, 11:32 am - Syam: int GetAnswer(int N, int M, string S, string T) {
    // Write your code here
    vector<vector<int>> pos(256);
    for (int i = 0; i < N; i++) pos[S[i]].push_back(i);
    int j = 0;
    for (int i = 0; i < N && j < M; i++) {
        if (S[i] == T[j]) j++;
    }
    if (j < M) return 0;
    int min_span = INT_MAX;
    vector<int> starts = pos[T[0]];
    for (int start_index : starts) {
        int curr = start_index;
        bool valid = true;
        for (int idx = 1; idx < M; idx++) {
            vector<int> lst = pos[T[idx]];
            auto it = upper_bound(lst.begin(), lst.end(), curr);
            if (it == lst.end()) {
                valid = false;
                break;;
            }
            curr = *it;
        }
        if (valid) {
            int span = curr - start_index;
            if (span < min_span) min_span = span;
        }
    }
    return  N + M - min_span - 1;
}
